  <span id="freeText12759055320613978797" style="display:none">This a taut, suspenseful murder mystery, set in Seattle, Washington. It is book 4 in the series, but I thought it worked ok as a stand alone. The book opens with the discovery of a woman's body in Puget Sound, by a man doing some out of season crabbing. The book switches back and forth between the police investigation and the thoughts of a missing woman at the center of this mystery. Tracy Crosswhite is the detective in charge of the case. She does not get along very well with her boss, Captain Nolasco. She has issues explained in one of the previous books in the series.<br /> There are many twists and turns in the case, with the thoughts of of the missing woman leading the reader in one direction and the police investigation in another. I did not suspect the killer until near the end. <br />Some quotes-- <br />Seattle PD bureaucracy: "After a $1.6 million investment, SPD had the facial recognition software and staff trained to use it, but the Seattle City Council had only approved its use to go through booking mug shots. DOL [Dept of Licenses]had the most comprehensive database of photographs of Washington residents, but the powers that be would not allow SPD to use that database to hunt down criminals because an ACLU lawyer had argued it could invade John Q. Citizen's privacy rights."<br />Weather "The hottest summer I ever spent was a winter in Phoenix."<br />This is a solid police procedural and I rate it a solid 4 out of 5 stars. Thanks to NetGalley and the publisher for sending me this ebook.</span>

<div id="review_2953011115" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2953011115" />
    <a title="Darryl Greer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3891082-darryl-greer"><img alt="Darryl Greer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445138545p2/3891082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2953011115?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darryl Greer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darryl Greer" href="/user/show/3891082-darryl-greer">Darryl Greer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2953011115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11613328160143524722">"The Trapped Girl" is fourth in author, Robert Dugoni’s Tracy Crosswhite series. The story gets off to a cracking start when a crab fisherman stumbles upon a crab pot in the chilly waters of Puget Sound off Seattle. Trouble is, it wasn’t filled with crabs, but a woman’s body. Tracy and her colleagues at the Seattle Police Department’s Violent Crimes Section are handed the case but have a troubling start when they find it difficult to identify the victim. It appears from her autopsy that she has </span>
  <span id="freeText11613328160143524722" style="display:none">"The Trapped Girl" is fourth in author, Robert Dugoni’s Tracy Crosswhite series. The story gets off to a cracking start when a crab fisherman stumbles upon a crab pot in the chilly waters of Puget Sound off Seattle. Trouble is, it wasn’t filled with crabs, but a woman’s body. Tracy and her colleagues at the Seattle Police Department’s Violent Crimes Section are handed the case but have a troubling start when they find it difficult to identify the victim. It appears from her autopsy that she has gone to great lengths to conceal her identity. When evidence comes to light that the unidentified woman could be a person who had disappeared some months earlier, Tracy is haunted by the memory of her own sister’s unsolved murder. One by one the clues are uncovered, but as they are, the mystery seems to deepen. And there’s a shock – and grave danger – for Tracy when the real culprit is eventually identified.<br /><br />Despite the promising start and an exciting dénouement in "The Trapped Girl", I could not describe this book as a thriller, more a plodding whodunit. I acknowledge and respect Robert Dugoni as a NYT bestselling author but the description on Amazon’s website, “a taut, riveting thriller” just doesn’t cut it for me. There were just too many parts of the narrative sandwiched between the opening and closing parts of the story that had me drifting off to other things jockeying for position in my mind. "The Trapped Girl" is worth a read, but more for lovers of murder/mystery novels.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11613328160143524722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11694495052217435707" style="display:none">I have just recently found Robert Dugoni's Tracy Whitecross series. <div id="review_1780378541" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1780378541" />
    <a title="Sandy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24770184-sandy"><img alt="Sandy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385133529p2/24770184.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1780378541?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy" href="/user/show/24770184-sandy">Sandy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24770184-sandy?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24770184-sandy?shelf=arc-from-netgalley">arc-from-netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24770184-sandy?shelf=detectives">detectives</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24770184-sandy?shelf=police-procedural">police-procedural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24770184-sandy?shelf=family-drama">family-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24770184-sandy?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24770184-sandy?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24770184-sandy?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24770184-sandy?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1780378541" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11021919737791335120">Poor Kurt Schill. All the kid wanted was to make a little money by setting a few crab pots in Puget Sound. After sneaking out one night to retrieve them, he thinks he may have hit the jackpot. One in particular has him struggling & when he finally gets it out of the water……is that a hand?<br/><br/>All together now….eeeewwww. Tracy & Kins feel the same way when they’re sent to collect the woman’s body. The autopsy provides clues that lead to her being identified as Lynn Hoff but there is surprisingly littl</span>
  <span id="freeText11021919737791335120" style="display:none">Poor Kurt Schill. All the kid wanted was to make a little money by setting a few crab pots in Puget Sound. After sneaking out one night to retrieve them, he thinks he may have hit the jackpot. One in particular has him struggling &amp; when he finally gets it out of the water……is that a hand?<br /><br />All together now….eeeewwww. Tracy &amp; Kins feel the same way when they’re sent to collect the woman’s body. The autopsy provides clues that lead to her being identified as Lynn Hoff but there is surprisingly little else to be found. <br /><br />Alternate chapters flash back to a year ago &amp; introduce us to Andrea Strickland. She’s a young, bookish woman in a new relationship that progresses as she tells her story. She’s had a tough life &amp; it’s about to get tougher. <br /><br />In the present Tracy &amp; her team have little to go on &amp; what they do find doesn’t seem to fit. Just when they make some headway, another precinct swoops in &amp; steals their case. Tracy is less than impressed for 2 reasons. First, she doesn’t feel like her boss (&amp; old nemesis) Johnny Nolasco fought hard enough to keep it. Second, the lead detective from the other precinct is a middle aged burnout more interested in “investigating” any women in his vicinity than actually doing his job.<br /><br />Boy, is this a snarly one. Just when you think you know where it’s going, another twist gets thrown out &amp; the story heads off in a new direction. It’s an intricate plot where there are few winners &amp; Tracy has to resort to some creative detecting to get the job done. It’s the kind of book where it’s important you don’t know too much ahead of time to fully appreciate the twists so that’s all I’ll say about the story. Except…thank God she’s maintained her sharpshooting skills.<br /><br />Andrea’s story is compelling &amp; chapters narrated in her voice become addictive reading. As events spiral out of control it’s easy to sympathize with this intelligent woman who yearns for a life very different from the one she has with her husband. All I’ll say about him is you’ll find his picture in the dictionary under “git”.<br /><br />This is book #4 &amp; one of the things I really enjoy about this series is the cast of characters that surround the MC. The other detectives are so well defined as individuals &amp; it’s a pleasure to read a police procedural where the members of a team actually like each other instead of spending all their time looking for a back to stab. There are also developments in Tracy’s personal life that hint at more changes in the future. <br /><br />It’s a smart, fast paced &amp; well plotted story that will keep you on your toes while reuniting fans with characters that have become old friends. Can’t wait for book #5.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11021919737791335120" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12412655610996090543" style="display:none">Clever and surprising, this fourth instalment in the Tracy Crosswhite series continues to keep the tension high and the reader hooked.         rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28393395-petra?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28393395-petra?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1776338855" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7103309085504489485">This is the thrilling fourth novel in the Tracy Crosswhite series. Tracy is a detective in Seattle PD's Violent Crimes Section and is facing her most complex case yet when a woman's body is recovered from a crab pot in the waters of Puget Sound. Identification initially proves difficult, but some clues lead Tracy and her team to believe they have discovered Andrea Strickland, who disappeared after climbing Liberty Ridge in Mount Rainier National Park with her husband Graham, a sleazy lawyer. But</span>
  <span id="freeText7103309085504489485" style="display:none">This is the thrilling fourth novel in the Tracy Crosswhite series. Tracy is a detective in Seattle PD's Violent Crimes Section and is facing her most complex case yet when a woman's body is recovered from a crab pot in the waters of Puget Sound. Identification initially proves difficult, but some clues lead Tracy and her team to believe they have discovered Andrea Strickland, who disappeared after climbing Liberty Ridge in Mount Rainier National Park with her husband Graham, a sleazy lawyer. But things just don't add up. <br />The story alternates between providing the reader with first-person POV background on Andrea Strickland and Tracy's investigation. Twists and turns galore combined with taut writing, enjoyable dialogue, and solid characterization - not only of the main players but the entire team behind Tracy - made this another compelling read in this series. I've been addicted to this since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22341263.My_Sister_s_Grave__Tracy_Crosswhite___1_" title="My Sister's Grave (Tracy Crosswhite, #1) by Robert Dugoni" rel="nofollow noopener">My Sister's Grave</a>, the first in the series, and am already looking forward to the release of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33845132.Close_to_Home__Tracy_Crosswhite___5_" title="Close to Home (Tracy Crosswhite, #5) by Robert Dugoni" rel="nofollow noopener">Close to Home</a> later this year.<br />I received an ARC via NetGalley. I purchased the audiobook which was once again narrated superbly by Emily Sutton-Smith.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7103309085504489485" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2090614062" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2090614062" />
    <a title="L.A. Starks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5159766-l-a-starks"><img alt="L.A. Starks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442453574p2/5159766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2090614062?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="L.A. Starks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="L.A. Starks" href="/user/show/5159766-l-a-starks">L.A. Starks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2090614062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10944621881816392661">This is a well-plotted Seattle-set mystery, fourth in the Tracey Crosswhite series. It opens with a great crab-catching scene. Dugoni has said he wanted to write a mystery with Mount Rainier as a setting and this book delivers. He also weaves in a ripped-from-the-headlines subplot about the business of selling marijuana--a business that turns out to be surprisingly competitive.<br/><br/>Most of all, Dugoni creates great empathy, with just the right curl of suspicion, about the title character of the book.</span>
  <span id="freeText10944621881816392661" style="display:none">This is a well-plotted Seattle-set mystery, fourth in the Tracey Crosswhite series. It opens with a great crab-catching scene. Dugoni has said he wanted to write a mystery with Mount Rainier as a setting and this book delivers. He also weaves in a ripped-from-the-headlines subplot about the business of selling marijuana--a business that turns out to be surprisingly competitive.<br /><br />Most of all, Dugoni creates great empathy, with just the right curl of suspicion, about the title character of the book.<br /><br />Okay, publishers, enough already with the diminutive of 'girl' in book titles. Authors are writing about capable, interesting, and experienced women. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10944621881816392661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

The detective in charge of that case is a misogynistic jerk determined to retain the case. Tracy does not let that stop h</span>
  <span id="freeText6571777788721074777" style="display:none">This is the 4th offering in the popular Tracy Crosswhite police procedural series and it is filled with twists and turns. It all begins when a teenage crab poacher’s pot snags another crab pot containing a dead body. The Seattle Police Department’s team has difficulty confirming the identity of the woman, but it seems related to a missing persons case in another jurisdiction. The detective in charge of that case is a misogynistic jerk determined to retain the case. Tracy does not let that stop her, she is undeterred in following every lead—no matter where it takes her. Enjoy!</span>

<div id="review_1840842074" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1840842074" />
    <a title="Sean Peters" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14058345-sean-peters"><img alt="Sean Peters" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579026851p2/14058345.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1840842074?book_show_action=true">Dec 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Peters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Peters" href="/user/show/14058345-sean-peters">Sean Peters</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1840842074" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5467189857211637504">Thank you to Net Galley, the publishers and the author for an ARC copy for an honest review.<br/><br/>The teenage Kurt Schill is engaging in illegal crab fishing in the cold waters of the Puget Sound. He is shocked to discover the dead body of a woman which the crabs have fed on in one of his crab pots.<br/><br/>Detective Tracy Crosswhite finds herself with a tough case to untangle. Before they can identify the killer, Tracy and her colleagues on the Seattle PD’s Violent Crimes Section must figure out who the victi</span>
  <span id="freeText5467189857211637504" style="display:none">Thank you to Net Galley, the publishers and the author for an ARC copy for an honest review.<br /><br />The teenage Kurt Schill is engaging in illegal crab fishing in the cold waters of the Puget Sound. He is shocked to discover the dead body of a woman which the crabs have fed on in one of his crab pots.<br /><br />Detective Tracy Crosswhite finds herself with a tough case to untangle. Before they can identify the killer, Tracy and her colleagues on the Seattle PD’s Violent Crimes Section must figure out who the victim is. Her autopsy, however, reveals she may have gone to great lengths to conceal her identity.<br /><br /> So who was she running from?<br /><br />After evidence surfaces that their Jane Doe may be a woman who suspiciously disappeared months earlier, Tracy is once again haunted by the memory of her sister’s unsolved murder. Dredging up details from the woman’s past leads to conflicting clues that only seem to muddy the investigation. As Tracy begins to uncover a twisted tale of brutal betrayal and desperate greed, she’ll find herself risking everything to confront a killer who won’t go down without a deadly fight.<br /><br />This is my first novel/book from New York Times bestselling author Robert Dugoni and here he delivers a taut, riveting thriller in the fourth installment of his acclaimed Tracy Crosswhite series, although my first book from this author and my first Tracey Crosswhite I loved this character and all her team.<br /><br />Robert Dugoni, has a collection of powerful, strong characters that make this book so much better, with a very clever plot that has you thinking all the way and shocks you where it does go in the end.<br /><br />The story was very interesting with a plot that really could lead anywhere. Full of tension and clever plotting and some lovely characters, who is guilty?<br /><br />A great read and another great author to keep us with. Four Stars. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5467189857211637504" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!

      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vEhQHeh8vw7ymevys/hvv1cC4Ez9sKqZln6ov/J+MgrWkLubIRi/3tK3d8aAoHfp0HM7QsW+wzhrjh8luwvE5Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('957KAt/ZFbd7CDTVqUS23teA9mTRYCXaN7AWpS8YrpKdRiGEFr0VZ1smqOGaHK6IUPEtauluTHvKQKE/Zm1YfQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2611372509151040674">Robert Dugoni is the New York Times, #1 Amazon, and #1 Wall Street Journal Bestselling Author of the Tracy Crosswhite series: My Sister's Grave, Her Last Breath, In the Clearing, The Trapped Girl and Close to Home, A Steep Price and A Cold Trail as well as the short prequels The Academy and Third Watch. The police procedural featuring Seattle Homicide Detective Tracy Crosswhite has kept Dugoni in </span>
  <span id="freeText2611372509151040674" style="display:none">Robert Dugoni is the New York Times, #1 Amazon, and #1 Wall Street Journal Bestselling Author of the Tracy Crosswhite series: My Sister's Grave, Her Last Breath, In the Clearing, The Trapped Girl and Close to Home, A Steep Price and A Cold Trail as well as the short prequels The Academy and Third Watch. The police procedural featuring Seattle Homicide Detective Tracy Crosswhite has kept Dugoni in the Amazon top 10 for more than three years and sold more than 5 million copies. He is also the author of the critically acclaimed The Extraordinary Life of Sam Hell, released April 2018 and soon to be a major motion picture. He is also the author of the Charles Jenkin's International spy series, The Eighth Sister and The Last Agent, soon to be a television series. Dugoni's first series featured attorney David Sloane and CIA agent Charles Jenkins. <br />He is the winner of the Nancy Pearl Award for fiction, a two-time nominee for the Harper Lee Award for Legal Fiction, A two-time nominee for the Mystery Writer's of America Edgar Award and a two-time nominee for the International Thriller of the year. His non-fiction expose, The Cyanide Canary, was a 2004 Best Book of the Year. He is published in more than 30 countries and two dozen languages.<br />You can sign up for his newsletter at:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.robertdugoni.com">http://www.robertdugoni.com</a> and message him on facebook, twitter and instagram </span>
  <a data-text-id="2611372509151040674" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
